💬 Response (24,825 in / 2,129 out)
Congratulations on your first baby! Here's a clear, step-by-step guide to everything you need to do and when:

---

## 🗓️ RIGHT NOW (Before the Birth — You Have 6 Weeks)

### 1. 📋 Check Your Maternity/Paternity Leave & Pay Entitlement
Use the GOV.UK checker tool to find out what you and your partner are entitled to:
👉 [Check Maternity or Paternity Leave or Pay](https://www.gov.uk/maternity-paternity-pay-leave)

You'll need your due date and employment details. This covers:
- **Statutory Maternity Leave** (up to 52 weeks) and **Statutory Maternity Pay** (SMP) — if you're an employee
- **Maternity Allowance** — if you're self-employed or don't qualify for SMP
- **Statutory Paternity Leave & Pay** — for your partner

> ⚠️ **Important:** You must notify your employer of your maternity leave **at least 15 weeks before your due date** — that deadline may already be very close for you! Do this immediately if you haven't already.

---

### 2. 💊 Get Your Maternity Exemption Certificate (MATEX)
As a pregnant woman, you're entitled to **free NHS prescriptions and free NHS dental treatment** — both during pregnancy and for 12 months after the birth. Ask your midwife or GP for a **FW8 form** to apply for your Maternity Exemption Certificate. This is free and worth doing straight away if you haven't already.

---

### 3. 💰 Apply for the Sure Start Maternity Grant (if eligible)
This is a **one-off, tax-free payment of £500** to help with the costs of your first baby.
👉 [Sure Start Maternity Grant](https://www.gov.uk/sure-start-maternity-grant)

**Eligibility:** You must be receiving one of these benefits: **Universal Credit, Income Support, income-based JSA, income-related ESA, or Pension Credit**.

> ⏰ **Deadline:** You can claim from **11 weeks before your due date** up to **6 months after the birth**. Since you're 6 weeks away, you can apply **now**. Don't miss this window!

*(Note: Not available in Scotland — apply for the Pregnancy and Baby Payment instead.)*

---

## 🏥 AT THE HOSPITAL / IMMEDIATELY AFTER THE BIRTH

### 4. Receive Your Baby's "Red Book"
The hospital or midwife will give you your baby's **Personal Child Health Record (the "red book")**. Keep this safe — you'll need it for health appointments and when registering the birth.

---

## 📅 WITHIN 42 DAYS OF THE BIRTH (Legal Requirement)

### 5. ✅ Register the Birth — **This Must Come First**
You are **legally required** to register your baby's birth within **42 days** in England, Wales, and Northern Ireland.
👉 [Register a birth](https://www.gov.uk/register-birth)

- Go to the **local register office** for the area where the baby was born (or sometimes at the hospital before you leave — ask the hospital staff)
- You'll need: date/place of birth, baby's name, parents' names, addresses, dates of birth, and occupations
- Bring ID (passport, birth certificate, or driving licence)
- Take the baby's red book as some registrars may ask for it

> ✅ **You must do this before you can claim Child Benefit.**

---

## 📅 WITHIN 48 HOURS OF REGISTERING THE BIRTH

### 6. 💷 Claim Child Benefit
Once the birth is registered, you can claim **Child Benefit** 48 hours later.
👉 [Claim Child Benefit](https://www.gov.uk/child-benefit/make-a-claim)

- Currently **£26.05/week** for your first child (2024/25 rate)
- Claim online — you'll need the birth certificate, your National Insurance number, and bank details
- **Can be backdated up to 3 months**, so don't delay
- Decide carefully **who claims** — the claimant receives National Insurance credits towards their State Pension (important if one of you isn't working)
- ⚠️ If either of you earns over £60,000/year, you may be subject to the **High Income Child Benefit Charge**

---

## 📅 LONGER TERM (After the Birth)

### 7. 🧾 Check for Additional Benefits
Depending on your income, you may also be entitled to:
- **Universal Credit** (if on a low income) — [Check eligibility](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit)
- **Free NHS Healthy Start vouchers** (for food and vitamins if on certain benefits)
- **Tax-Free Childcare** — when you return to work, you can get up to £500/quarter towards childcare costs: [Tax-Free Childcare](https://www.gov.uk/tax-free-childcare)

---

## ✅ Summary Checklist

| When | What to Do |
|---|---|
| **Now (urgent!)** | Notify employer of maternity leave (if not done) |
| **Now** | Get Maternity Exemption Certificate (MATEX) from midwife/GP |
| **Now** | Apply for Sure Start Maternity Grant (if on qualifying benefits) |
| **Within 42 days of birth** | Register the birth at the register office |
| **48hrs after registering** | Claim Child Benefit online |
| **After birth** | Check Universal Credit / other benefit entitlements |
| **When returning to work** | Look into Tax-Free Childcare |

---

Is there anything specific you'd like more detail on — for example, maternity pay, benefits, or childcare options?

Congratulations on your upcoming arrival! 🎉 Here's a comprehensive, time-ordered guide to everything you need to do and when.

---

## 🤰 Right Now — Before the Birth (You have 6 weeks)

### 1. 📋 Maternity Exemption Certificate (MatEx)
**Ask your midwife or GP for this at your next appointment.** It gives you free NHS prescriptions and free dental treatment throughout your pregnancy and for **12 months after the birth**. Ask for the **FW8 form** — the certificate is then posted to you automatically.
- 📞 NHS BSA: 0300 330 1341 (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm, Sat 9am–3pm)

### 2. 💰 Sort out your maternity/paternity pay — NOW
You need to notify your employer before the birth:

- **Statutory Maternity Pay (SMP)** — if you've worked for the same employer for 26+ weeks by the 15th week before your due date. Paid for up to 39 weeks: first 6 weeks at 90% of your average earnings, then **£187.18/week** for 33 weeks. You'll need your **MATB1 certificate** from your midwife.
- **Maternity Allowance** — if you're self-employed, recently changed jobs, or not eligible for SMP. Also up to 39 weeks at **£187.18/week**. Apply via [GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/maternity-allowance/how-to-claim).
- **Statutory Paternity Pay (SPP)** — for the baby's father or partner. 1–2 weeks at **£187.18/week**. ⚠️ Must be arranged **before the baby is 8 weeks old**.
- 📞 HMRC: 0300 200 3300 (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm)

### 3. 💷 Sure Start Maternity Grant — Apply Now if Eligible
If you're on a qualifying benefit (e.g. Universal Credit, Income Support), you can claim a **one-off £500 payment**. You can apply from **11 weeks before your due date**, so you can do this right now! ⚠️ Deadline: 3 months after birth. Usually first child only.
- 📞 Jobcentre Plus: 0800 169 0140 (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm)
- Apply via [GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/sure-start-maternity-grant/how-to-claim)

### 4. 🥦 Healthy Start Vouchers — Apply if Eligible
If you're 10+ weeks pregnant and on qualifying benefits, you can get a **prepaid card worth £8.50/week** to spend on fruit, vegetables, milk and infant formula. This continues after the birth (£4.25/week per child under 1).
- Apply at [healthystart.nhs.uk](https://www.healthystart.nhs.uk/how-to-apply/)
- 📞 0300 330 7010 (Mon–Fri 9am–5pm)

---

## 👶 Within 42 Days of the Birth — Critical Deadline

### 5. 🏛️ Register the Birth *(Legal requirement — 42-day deadline)*
You **must** register your baby at your **local register office** in person. This is the gateway to almost everything else. Bring:
- The hospital notification of birth
- Both parents' ID

👉 [Find your nearest register office](https://www.gov.uk/register-offices)

---

## 📅 Shortly After the Birth

### 6. 👶 Claim Child Benefit — Do This Promptly
Worth **£26.05/week** for your first child. Can be backdated up to 3 months, so don't delay too long. You'll need the birth certificate from step 5.
- ⚠️ If either parent earns over £60,000, the High Income Child Benefit Charge applies — but it's still worth claiming to protect your **National Insurance record**.
- Apply online at [GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/child-benefit/how-to-claim) (requires Government Gateway login)
- 📞 Child Benefit helpline: 0300 200 3100 (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm)

### 7. 🏖️ Consider Shared Parental Leave (SPL)
If both parents are eligible (both must meet employment and earnings tests), you can share up to **50 weeks of leave and 37 weeks of pay** between you at **£187.18/week**. Both employers need to be notified. Plan this early as it requires advance notice.
- 📞 HMRC: 0300 200 3300

### 8. 💳 Order Extra Birth Certificates
You'll likely need certified copies for things like passport applications, insurance, etc. Each costs **£11**.
- Order online at [GRO](https://www.gro.gov.uk/gro/content/certificates/default.asp)
- 📞 GRO: 0300 123 1837 (Mon–Fri 8am–8pm, Sat 9am–4pm)

---

## 📅 When Your Baby is Older — Plan Ahead

### 9. 🧒 Free Childcare — 15 Hours (from 9 months old)
A **universal entitlement** — no income test. From the term after your baby turns 9 months, they're entitled to **15 hours/week of free childcare**. Apply via your Government Gateway account.
- 📞 Childcare Service helpline: 0300 123 4097

### 10. 🧒 Free Childcare — 30 Hours (3–4 year olds)
If both parents work at least 16 hours/week at National Minimum Wage and neither earns over £100,000, your child will be entitled to **30 hours/week** of free childcare from age 3.

### 11. 💰 Tax-Free Childcare Account
For every **£8 you pay in**, the government adds **£2** (up to £500/quarter per child). Cannot be used alongside the Universal Credit childcare element — compare both to see which is better for you.
- Apply at [GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/tax-free-childcare)

---

## 💡 Other Things That May Apply to You

Depending on your circumstances, you may also be eligible for:

| Service | Who it's for |
|---|---|
| **Universal Credit** | If you're on a low income or out of work — a new baby is a change of circumstances to report |
| **Council Tax Reduction** | If on low income — apply to your local council |
| **NHS Low Income Scheme (HC2/HC3)** | If not on benefits but on a low income — helps with prescriptions, dental and sight tests |
| **NI Credits** | Automatically protects your State Pension record if you're on UC or claiming Child Benefit |
| **Help to Save** | If on UC — government adds a 50% bonus to your savings (up to £1,200 total) |

---

## 🗺️ Your Timeline at a Glance

| When | What to do |
|---|---|
| **Now (6 weeks before birth)** | Get MatEx certificate, notify employer of maternity/paternity leave, apply for Sure Start Grant (if eligible), apply for Healthy Start (if eligible) |
| **Within 42 days of birth** | ⚠️ Register the birth |
| **Soon after birth** | Claim Child Benefit, arrange Paternity Leave (within 8 weeks), order extra birth certificates |
| **Baby aged 9 months** | Apply for 15 hours free childcare |
| **Baby aged 3** | Apply for 30 hours free childcare |

---

Would you like more detail on any of these — for example, help working out whether you're eligible for SMP or Maternity Allowance, or how to claim Child Benefit?

💬 Response (38,432 in / 2,418 out)
Excellent — I now have everything I need to give you a thorough and accurate answer. Here's a full breakdown of the additional benefits relevant to your situation:

---

## 💰 Additional Benefits for Low-Income Families with a Self-Employed Partner

---

### 1. 🏦 Universal Credit — **Apply Now / As Soon As Possible**
👉 [Universal Credit](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit)

This is likely your most significant source of additional support. As a low-income household, you can claim even if one or both of you are working or self-employed.

**You're eligible if:**
- You're on a low income (working, self-employed, or out of work)
- You have **£16,000 or less** in savings/investments combined
- You're both UK residents aged 18+

**As a couple, you must make a joint claim.** Your partner's self-employment income will be taken into account, but Universal Credit is designed to support working people on low incomes too.

**What you could get on top of the standard allowance:**
| Extra Element | Monthly Amount |
|---|---|
| Standard couple allowance (one or both 25+) | **£628.10** |
| Child element (first child, born on/after 6 April 2017) | **+£292.81** |
| Childcare costs (up to 85% back when working) | Up to **£1,031.88/month** |

> ⚠️ **Important for self-employed partners:** Universal Credit uses a **Minimum Income Floor** — it assumes your partner earns at least the equivalent of the minimum wage for their hours. However, this is **suspended for the first 12 months** of self-employment, and also during periods of illness or caring responsibilities. A work coach can advise on this.

---

### 2. 🤱 Maternity Allowance (for you) — **Apply Now, if not already done**
👉 [Maternity Allowance](https://www.gov.uk/maternity-allowance)

Since you mentioned you're on a low income, it's worth confirming whether you qualify for **Statutory Maternity Pay (SMP)** from your employer, or whether you need **Maternity Allowance** instead. Maternity Allowance is paid by the government (not your employer) and covers:
- Employed people who don't qualify for SMP
- Self-employed people
- People who recently stopped working

**Eligibility:** You must have been employed or self-employed for at least **26 of the 66 weeks** before your due date, earning at least **£30/week** in at least 13 of those weeks.

**You can apply now** — as soon as you've been pregnant for 26 weeks. Don't wait until the birth!

---

### 3. 👨 Your Partner's Paternity Leave & Pay — **Important Caveat for Self-Employed**
👉 [Paternity Pay and Leave](https://www.gov.uk/paternity-pay-leave)

Unfortunately, **Statutory Paternity Pay is only available to employees**, not the self-employed. To qualify, your partner would need to:
- Be an **employee** (not self-employed)
- Have worked for their employer for at least **26 weeks** up to the 15th week before the due date
- Earn at least **£125/week** on average

Since your partner is self-employed, they are **not entitled to Statutory Paternity Pay**. However, they can of course choose to take time off — their income during that period would simply depend on their business. Universal Credit could help bridge this gap.

---

### 4. 🥦 Healthy Start Vouchers — **Apply Now**
👉 [Healthy Start](https://www.gov.uk/healthy-start)

If you're claiming **Universal Credit** (or certain other qualifying benefits), you can get **Healthy Start prepaid cards** to spend on:
- Milk
- Fresh and frozen fruit and vegetables
- Fresh, dried, and tinned pulses
- Infant formula milk

**Eligibility:** You must be more than 10 weeks pregnant **and** receiving a qualifying benefit such as Universal Credit. *(Note: Not available in Scotland — apply for Best Start Foods instead.)*

> ✅ Apply for this **at the same time** as Universal Credit, or as soon as your UC claim is confirmed.

---

### 5. 🆓 Free NHS Vitamins
Through the Healthy Start scheme, you can also get **free vitamins** — folic acid and vitamin D for you during pregnancy, and vitamin D drops for your baby. Ask your midwife or health visitor how to access these.

---

### 6. 🏠 Housing Benefit / Help with Rent
If you're renting, Universal Credit includes a **housing element** to help with rent costs. Make sure you include your rent details when you apply. The amount depends on your local housing allowance rate.

---

### 7. 🧮 Use a Benefits Calculator First
Before applying, it's worth running your numbers through a free, anonymous benefits calculator to get an estimate of everything you're entitled to:
👉 [Benefits Calculators on GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/benefits-calculators)

Recommended calculators:
- **[Turn2us](https://benefits-calculator.turn2us.org.uk/)** — very family-friendly
- **[Entitledto](https://www.entitledto.co.uk/)** — good for self-employed households
- **[Policy in Practice](https://betteroffcalculator.co.uk/)** — shows how changes in income affect your benefits

---

## ✅ Your Priority Action List

| Priority | Action | When |
|---|---|---|
| 🔴 **Urgent** | Apply for **Maternity Allowance** (if not already done) | Now — you're 6 weeks from due date |
| 🔴 **Urgent** | Run a **benefits calculator** to estimate your UC entitlement | Now |
| 🔴 **Urgent** | Apply for **Universal Credit** as a couple | Now |
| 🟡 **Soon after** | Apply for **Healthy Start vouchers** | Once UC is confirmed |
| 🟡 **Soon after** | Confirm **Sure Start Maternity Grant** (£500) — now you're on UC, you'll qualify! | Now — up to 6 months after birth |
| 🟢 **After birth** | Report the new baby to DWP to add the **child element** to your UC | Within 1 month of birth |

---

> 💡 **Key tip:** Once you're on Universal Credit, you'll automatically qualify for the **Sure Start Maternity Grant** (£500 one-off payment mentioned in my earlier advice), so if you haven't applied yet, get your UC claim in first, then apply for the grant straight away!

💬 Response (87,584 in / 2,559 out)
Excellent — I now have a very detailed picture of everything relevant to your situation. Here's a focused guide on the **additional support available to you as a low-income household with a self-employed partner**:

---

## 💰 Additional Support for Low-Income Families with a Self-Employed Partner

---

### 🌟 THE BIG ONE: Universal Credit (UC)

**This is the most important thing to look into.** As a low-income household expecting a baby, Universal Credit is likely your gateway to a whole range of other support.

**What you could get:**
| Element | Amount (2025-26) |
|---|---|
| Standard couple allowance (both 25+) | **£628.10/month** |
| Child element (first child) | **+£333.33/month** |
| Childcare costs element | Up to **85% of childcare costs** |
| Housing element | Covers eligible rent costs |

**Key eligibility checks:**
- ✅ You must be 18+, UK resident, and on a low income
- ✅ Savings must be **under £16,000** (savings between £6,000–£16,000 reduce your award)
- ✅ As a couple, you'll make a **joint claim**
- ⚠️ Your partner being self-employed is fine — UC has a "minimum income floor" for self-employed people, but this is **suspended for the first 12 months** of self-employment, and also during periods of sickness/caring

**What to prepare:**
- Photo ID for both of you
- Both NI numbers
- 3 months' bank statements
- Proof of address
- Details of any rent/mortgage

👉 **Claim online:** [gov.uk/universal-credit/how-to-claim](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit/how-to-claim)
📞 **Helpline:** 0800 328 5644 (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm)

> ⚠️ **Important:** If you're already on any legacy benefits (Tax Credits, Housing Benefit, Income Support), do **not** switch to UC without taking advice first — contact Citizens Advice or call the UC helpline.

---

### 🤰 Maternity Allowance — For Your Self-Employed Partner (if applicable) or You

Since your partner is self-employed, **Statutory Maternity Pay (SMP) won't apply to them**. If *you* are the one who is pregnant and self-employed or not eligible for SMP, **Maternity Allowance** is your route:

- **£187.18/week for up to 39 weeks**
- Requires: worked at least **26 weeks** in the 66 weeks before your due date, and earned at least **£30/week** for 13 of those weeks
- You'll need your **MATB1 certificate** from your midwife and evidence of self-employment (e.g. accounts, tax returns)

👉 **Apply:** [gov.uk/maternity-allowance/how-to-claim](https://www.gov.uk/maternity-allowance/how-to-claim)
📞 **Jobcentre Plus:** 0800 169 0140 (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm)

---

### 🏠 Council Tax Reduction — Apply to Your Local Council

On a low income, you could have your Council Tax bill **significantly reduced or eliminated entirely**. This is administered locally so the exact amount varies, but it's well worth applying — especially once you're on UC, which acts as a fast-track qualifier.

👉 **Find your council:** [gov.uk/find-local-council](https://www.gov.uk/find-local-council)

---

### 🍎 Healthy Start Vouchers — Apply Now!

If you're on UC (or other qualifying benefits) and 10+ weeks pregnant, you qualify for a **prepaid card worth £8.50/week now**, rising to **£4.25/week per child** after the birth, to spend on fruit, veg, milk and infant formula.

👉 **Apply:** [healthystart.nhs.uk/how-to-apply](https://www.healthystart.nhs.uk/how-to-apply/)
📞 0300 330 7010 (Mon–Fri 9am–5pm)

---

### 💷 Sure Start Maternity Grant — £500 One-Off Payment

If you're on UC or another qualifying benefit, you can claim a **one-off £500 grant** to help with costs for your new baby. As this is your first child, you should qualify.

⚠️ **You can apply NOW** (from 11 weeks before your due date) — don't wait until after the birth!
⚠️ Deadline: **3 months after the birth**

📞 **Jobcentre Plus:** 0800 169 0140 (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm)
👉 [gov.uk/sure-start-maternity-grant](https://www.gov.uk/sure-start-maternity-grant)

---

### 🧒 Free Childcare for Disadvantaged 2-Year-Olds *(England only)*

Once your baby turns 2, if you're on UC with an annual household income **under £15,400**, your child will be entitled to **15 hours/week of free childcare** — a full year earlier than the universal 15-hour entitlement at 9 months. This is on top of the universal entitlement.

👉 Apply through your local council when the time comes.

---

### 💾 Help to Save — Up to £1,200 Government Bonus

If you're on UC, you can open a **Help to Save account** and earn a **50% government bonus** on whatever you save:
- Save up to **£50/month** for up to 4 years
- Bonus paid at end of **year 2** (up to £600) and **year 4** (up to £600)
- Maximum total bonus: **£1,200**

Even saving a small amount each month adds up significantly with the 50% top-up. This is a great way to build an emergency fund.

👉 **Open an account:** [gov.uk/get-help-savings-low-income](https://www.gov.uk/get-help-savings-low-income)

---

### 🌐 Social Tariff Broadband

If you're on UC, you're eligible for **discounted broadband** from major providers (BT, Virgin Media, Sky, etc.) at typically **£12–20/month** — potentially saving you £30–40/month compared to standard tariffs.

👉 Check what's available: [gov.uk/affordable-broadband](https://www.gov.uk/affordable-broadband)

---

### 🏥 NHS Low Income Scheme (HC2 Certificate)

If you're not automatically getting free NHS services through benefits, the **HC2 certificate** gives you:
- ✅ Free NHS prescriptions
- ✅ Free NHS dental treatment
- ✅ Free NHS sight tests + optical vouchers
- ✅ Help with travel to hospital

> Note: Once you're on UC, many of these are automatic — but if there's any gap in coverage, the HC2 fills it.

👉 Apply with form HC1: [gov.uk/nhs-low-income-scheme](https://www.gov.uk/nhs-low-income-scheme)
📞 NHS BSA: 0300 330 1343

---

## 🗺️ Your Priority Action Plan

| Priority | Action | Why |
|---|---|---|
| 🔴 **Do now** | **Claim Universal Credit** (if not already) | Unlocks most other support |
| 🔴 **Do now** | **Apply for Sure Start Maternity Grant** | £500 one-off — deadline is 3 months after birth |
| 🔴 **Do now** | **Apply for Healthy Start vouchers** | £8.50/week free food now |
| 🔴 **Do now** | **Apply for Maternity Allowance** | £187.18/week for 39 weeks if self-employed/not eligible for SMP |
| 🟡 **Soon** | **Apply for Council Tax Reduction** | Could eliminate your council tax bill |
| 🟡 **Soon** | **Check social tariff broadband** | Save £30–40/month |
| 🟢 **After UC is set up** | **Open a Help to Save account** | 50% government bonus on savings |
| 🟢 **Baby turns 2** | **Apply for disadvantaged 2-year-old childcare** | 15 hrs/week free childcare a year early |

💬 Response (15,332 in / 811 out)
Based on the latest GOV.UK information, here's a clear answer:

---

## 👶 The Very First Thing to Do After the Baby is Born

### ✅ Step 1: Register the Birth — **Within 42 Days (Legal Requirement)**
👉 [Register a birth](https://www.gov.uk/register-birth)

This is the **single most important first step** — everything else (Child Benefit, Sure Start Maternity Grant, etc.) flows from this. You cannot claim most benefits until it's done.

**Where to go:**
- Your **local register office** for the area where the baby was born, OR
- **At the hospital** before you leave — ask the hospital staff if this is available, as it's the most convenient option

**What to bring:**
- At least one form of **photo ID** (passport, driving licence, or birth certificate)
- Proof of address (utility bill or Council Tax bill)
- Your baby's **red book** (personal child health record — given to you at the hospital)
- Your **marriage or civil partnership certificate** (if applicable)
- You'll need to know: the baby's name, date and place of birth, both parents' names, dates of birth, addresses, and occupations

---

### ✅ Step 2: Claim Child Benefit — **48 Hours After Registering**
You'll need the birth certificate in hand. Claim online as soon as possible — it can be backdated up to 3 months, but don't delay.

---

### ✅ Step 3: Apply for the Sure Start Maternity Grant — **As Soon As Possible After Birth**
Since you're on Universal Credit, you **will qualify** for this £500 one-off payment. The deadline is **6 months after the birth**, but apply as soon as you can.

---

### ✅ Step 4: Report the Baby to DWP for Universal Credit
Let the DWP know about your new baby to have the **child element (£292.81/month)** added to your Universal Credit payments. Do this **within 1 month** of the birth to avoid losing any payments.

---

> 💡 **In short:** The very first official thing to do is **register the birth** — ideally at the hospital before you even go home, if that option is available to you. Everything else follows from there!

Would you like help with anything else, such as what to do when you return to work, or how to apply for any of these benefits?

💬 Response (81,656 in / 789 out)
The answer is clear and confirmed by the official service data. Here's everything you need to know:

---

## 👶 The Very First Thing: **Register the Birth**

### ⚠️ This is a legal requirement — and it unlocks almost everything else

**Registering the birth is the single most important first step.** It's the gateway to Child Benefit, free childcare, the Sure Start Maternity Grant, and more. Nothing else can happen without it.

---

### 📋 What you need to do

**Go in person to your local register office.** You cannot do this online or by post — it must be done in person by a parent (or someone else present at the birth).

👉 **Find your nearest register office:** [gov.uk/register-offices](https://www.gov.uk/register-offices)

---

### 📁 What to bring

- ✅ The **hospital notification of birth** (given to you by the hospital or midwife)
- ✅ **Both parents' ID documents**
- ✅ Have your **baby's name decided** — it goes on the certificate

---

### ⏰ Deadline: **42 days from the date of birth**

Don't leave it too long — the sooner you register, the sooner you can claim Child Benefit (worth **£26.05/week**) and the Sure Start Maternity Grant (**£500 one-off**), both of which require the birth certificate.

---

### 🔓 What registering the birth unlocks

Once you have the birth certificate in hand, you can immediately move on to:

| Next step | Why it matters |
|---|---|
| **Child Benefit** | £26.05/week — claim ASAP, backdatable only 3 months |
| **Sure Start Maternity Grant** | £500 one-off — deadline is 3 months after birth |
| **Statutory Paternity Pay** | Must be arranged within **8 weeks** of birth |
| **Free childcare (15 hrs)** | From 9 months old — needs birth cert to apply |
| **Extra birth certificates** | Order copies at £11 each for insurance, passport, etc. |

---

### 📞 Need help?

**GRO certificate enquiries:** 0300 123 1837
- Mon–Fri: 8am–8pm
- Saturday: 9am–4pm

---

So in short: **as soon as you feel well enough after the birth, book your appointment at the register office.** Everything else flows from that one step. Would you like help planning what to do immediately after you've registered?

💬 Response (15,094 in / 1,857 out)
First of all, please accept my sincere condolences for the loss of your mother. Here is a clear, step-by-step guide to everything you need to do, based on the official GOV.UK guidance:

---

## What to Do When Someone Dies – Your Step-by-Step Guide

### ✅ STEP 1: Register the Death *(Do this first – everything else depends on it)*
**You must do this before anything else.**
- You need to register the death at a **local register office**, ideally in the district where she died.
- You'll need a **Medical Certificate of Cause of Death** from the doctor or hospital.
- This must usually be done **within 5 days** (England & Wales).
- You'll receive a **Death Certificate** – get several certified copies (you'll need them for banks, probate, etc.) and a **unique Tell Us Once reference number**.
- 👉 [Register a death – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/register-a-death)

---

### ✅ STEP 2: Use the "Tell Us Once" Service *(Do this within 28 days of registering)*
- This free government service lets you **notify multiple government departments in one go**, including HMRC, DWP, the Passport Office, DVLA, and your mother's local council.
- The registrar will give you a **unique reference number** to use the service online or by phone.
- It will cancel things like State Pension, benefits, Council Tax discounts, and her driving licence automatically.
- 👉 [Tell Us Once – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/tell-us-once)

---

### ✅ STEP 3: Arrange the Funeral
- This can happen alongside Step 2. A funeral director can help guide you.
- If you're struggling with costs, you may be able to apply for a **Funeral Expenses Payment** from the government.
- 👉 [Get help paying for a funeral – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/funeral-payments)

---

### ✅ STEP 4: Value the Estate & Check for Inheritance Tax *(Must happen BEFORE applying for probate)*
Because your mother **owned her home**, her estate will need to be valued. This includes:
- The property (you'll likely need a professional valuation)
- Savings, investments, and personal possessions
- Any debts she owed

**Inheritance Tax (IHT):**
- The threshold is currently **£325,000** (or up to £500,000 if the home passes to a direct descendant, using the Residence Nil Rate Band).
- If the estate is above the threshold, IHT is due at **40%** on the amount above it, and you must report it using **form IHT400** and begin paying **before** probate is granted.
- Even if no IHT is due, you still need the estate valuation for your probate application.
- 👉 [Value the estate and pay Inheritance Tax – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/valuing-estate-of-someone-who-died)

---

### ✅ STEP 5: Apply for Probate *(Required to deal with the property)*
Because your mother owned her home, **you will almost certainly need Probate** – this is the legal authority to deal with her estate.

- **If she left a will:** The named **executor(s)** apply for a **Grant of Probate**.
- **If she did not leave a will:** The closest living relative applies for **Letters of Administration**.
- You can apply **online or by post** after valuing the estate.
- The current fee is **£300** for estates over £5,000 (free under £5,000).
- ⚠️ **Do not put the property on the market until Probate is granted.**
- 👉 [Apply for probate – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/applying-for-probate)
- 📞 Courts & Tribunals Service Centre: **0300 303 0648** (Mon–Fri, 9am–1pm)

---

### ✅ STEP 6: Deal with the Estate
Once Probate is granted, you can:
- Access and close her bank accounts
- Sell or transfer the property
- Pay any outstanding debts or taxes
- Distribute what remains according to her will (or the rules of intestacy if there's no will)
- **Update the property records** at HM Land Registry
- 👉 [Deal with the estate – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/wills-probate-inheritance/dealing-with-the-estate)

---

### 📋 Also Don't Forget (Outside of Government):
- Notify her **bank(s)** and any building societies
- Contact her **mortgage provider** (if applicable) or landlord
- Cancel or redirect her **utilities, subscriptions, and insurance**
- Notify her **private pension providers**
- Secure the **property** (check insurance remains valid on an unoccupied home – many policies have time limits)

---

### 🔑 Key Dependency Summary:
> **Register death → Tell Us Once → Value estate → Apply for Probate → Deal with estate (including property)**

The full GOV.UK guide is here: [What to do when someone dies: step by step](https://www.gov.uk/when-someone-dies)

Please don't hesitate to ask if you'd like more detail on any of these steps. I'm here to help.

💬 Response (14,712 in / 1,603 out)
Thank you for your patience. I'm so sorry for your loss. Here is a clear, step-by-step guide to everything you need to do, in the right order.

---

## Your Bereavement Journey — What to Do and When

Because your mother owned her home, **probate will almost certainly be required**. Here's how everything fits together:

---

### 🔴 Phase 1 — Do These First (Gateway Steps)

#### 1. Register the Death ⏰ *Within 5 days*
This is the essential first step that unlocks everything else.
- Go **in person** to your local register office
- Bring the **Medical Certificate of Cause of Death (MCCD)** issued by the doctor/hospital
- A relative or someone present at the death can register it
- 📞 Find your nearest office: [gov.uk/register-offices](https://www.gov.uk/register-offices)

> **At the appointment**, ask to use **Tell Us Once** (see step 3) — it's offered on the spot.

---

#### 2. Order Multiple Death Certificates
- Banks, insurers, HMRC, and the probate service all need **original certified copies**
- **Order at least 5** — they cost £11 each
- You can order them at the register office or online via [GRO](https://www.gro.gov.uk/gro/content/certificates/default.asp)

---

#### 3. Use Tell Us Once
- This **notifies up to 23 government departments in one go** — HMRC, DVLA, DWP, Passport Office, your local council, and more
- Usually offered at the register office appointment, or do it online/by phone afterwards
- 📞 Helpline: **0800 085 7308** (Mon–Fri, 8am–6pm)
- 🔗 [gov.uk/after-a-death](https://www.gov.uk/after-a-death/organisations-you-need-to-contact-and-tell-us-once)

> Tell Us Once will automatically handle cancelling her driving licence and notifying the council.

---

#### 4. Check for Inheritance Tax (IHT) ⏰ *Tax due within 6 months of death*
Because your mother **owned her home**, her estate may exceed the tax-free threshold:
- **£325,000** standard nil-rate band
- **Up to £500,000** if the home is left to children/grandchildren (residence nil-rate band)
- If the estate exceeds the threshold, you must complete an **IHT400 form** and pay any tax **before probate is granted**
- 📞 HMRC Inheritance Tax helpline: **0300 123 1072** (Mon–Fri, 9am–5pm)
- 🔗 [gov.uk/inheritance-tax](https://www.gov.uk/inheritance-tax)

---

#### 5. Notify the Office of the Public Guardian (if applicable)
- If your mother had a **Lasting Power of Attorney (LPA)** in place, the attorneys must notify the OPG — the LPA automatically ceases on death
- Return the original LPA document with an LP4 form
- 📞 OPG: **0300 456 0300** (Mon–Fri, 9am–5pm)

---

### 🟡 Phase 2 — Once Death is Registered & IHT is Resolved

#### 6. Apply for Probate *(required for the property)*
Since your mother owned her home, **you will need a Grant of Probate** to deal with her estate (sell/transfer the property, access bank accounts, etc.).
- Apply online or by post using form **PA1P** (if there's a will) or **PA1A** (no will)
- You'll need: the will (if there is one), death certificate, and a valuation of the estate
- **Fee: £300** for estates over £5,000
- ⚠️ **Current processing time: 16+ weeks** — apply as soon as IHT is sorted
- 📞 Probate helpline: **0300 303 0648** (Mon–Fri, 8am–6pm)
- 🔗 [gov.uk/applying-for-probate](https://www.gov.uk/applying-for-probate)

---

### 💡 Other Things to Be Aware Of

| Service | Details |
|---|---|
| **Council Tax** | As your mother lived alone, her property may now be **exempt from Council Tax** while it's unoccupied and part of the estate. Contact her local council. |
| **Funeral Expenses Payment** | If *you* are on a qualifying benefit (Universal Credit, Pension Credit, etc.) and are paying for the funeral, you may claim up to £1,000 toward costs. ⏰ Claim within **6 months** of the funeral. 📞 0800 151 2012 |
| **Bereavement Support Payment** | Only applies if your *spouse or civil partner* died — not relevant here, but flagged in case. |
| **Statutory Parental Bereavement Leave** | If a **child under 18** in your care has died, you're entitled to 2 weeks' paid leave from your employer. Not applicable here, but noted. |

---

### 📋 Quick Checklist Summary

- [ ] Register the death at the register office (within 5 days)
- [ ] Order at least 5 certified death certificates (£11 each)
- [ ] Use Tell Us Once to notify government departments
- [ ] Value the estate and check if Inheritance Tax is due (pay within 6 months)
- [ ] Apply for Probate (needed to deal with the property)
- [ ] Notify OPG if an LPA existed
- [ ] Contact the local council about the property's Council Tax status

---

This is a lot to take on while grieving. You don't have to do it all at once — **registering the death and using Tell Us Once are the most urgent steps**. Would you like more detail on any of these, such as how to value the estate or what happens to the property during probate?

💬 Response (24,443 in / 1,829 out)
Yes, this does add meaningful complexity in two key areas: **UK Inheritance Tax reporting** and **dealing with the Spanish property separately under Spanish law**. Here's how it changes things:

---

## How Foreign Assets Affect What You Need to Do

### 💰 Impact on UK Inheritance Tax

Because your mother was **permanently resident in the UK**, **all of her worldwide assets** – including the Spanish property and any overseas savings – must be included in the UK estate valuation for Inheritance Tax purposes.

This means:
- The **Spanish property value** (converted to GBP at the date of death) must be added to the UK estate total
- Any **foreign savings or bank accounts** must also be included
- This makes it **more likely the estate will exceed the £325,000–£500,000 IHT threshold**, meaning IHT at 40% could be due
- You will need to complete **form IHT400** (the full Inheritance Tax return) **plus form IHT417 – "Foreign Assets"** as a supplementary form
- 👉 [IHT417 – Foreign Assets form – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/inheritance-tax-foreign-assets-iht417)

> ⚠️ **Important:** Any IHT owed on the foreign assets is still payable to **HMRC in the UK**, even though the assets are abroad. However, if Spain also charges inheritance tax on the property, you may be able to claim **double taxation relief** to avoid being taxed twice on the same asset. A solicitor experienced in cross-border estates can help with this.

---

### 🏠 The Spanish Property – A Separate Legal Process

This is the most significant complication. **A UK Grant of Probate is NOT automatically recognised in Spain.** The Spanish property must go through a **separate legal process under Spanish law**, regardless of what happens in the UK.

Here's what that typically involves:

1. **Apostille on the UK Death Certificate** – You'll need an official certified copy of the UK death certificate with an **Apostille stamp** (a form of international authentication), so it can be used in Spain.
- 👉 [Get a document legalised (Apostille) – GOV.UK](https://www.gov.uk/get-document-legalised)

2. **Spanish Inheritance Process ("Herencia")** – You will need to engage a **Spanish lawyer (abogado)** and likely a **Spanish notary (notario)** to handle the transfer of the property under Spanish inheritance law. This is a separate process from UK probate.

3. **Spanish Inheritance Tax ("Impuesto sobre Sucesiones")** – Spain charges its own inheritance tax on property located in Spain. The rate and any allowances vary by region (each autonomous community has different rules). As a non-resident heir, you may be taxed at national rates unless the regional rules apply. A Spanish lawyer can advise on this.

4. **Timescale** – Spain has a **6-month deadline** from the date of death to submit the inheritance declaration and pay Spanish inheritance tax, though extensions can sometimes be requested. **This deadline is tight**, so engaging a Spanish lawyer promptly is important.

5. **If there was a Spanish will** – If your mother made a separate will in Spain (which is common for people with Spanish property), this will govern the Spanish estate. If not, the UK will (or intestacy rules) will need to be translated and authenticated for use in Spain.

---

### 📋 Updated Order of Priority

Given the above, here's how your to-do list is updated:

| Priority | Action |
|----------|--------|
| 🔴 **Urgent** | Register the death & get multiple certified copies |
| 🔴 **Urgent** | Get an **Apostille** on the death certificate for use in Spain |
| 🔴 **Urgent** | **Engage a Spanish lawyer immediately** – the 6-month Spanish tax deadline is already running |
| 🟠 **Soon** | Use **Tell Us Once** |
| 🟠 **Soon** | Get the Spanish property professionally valued (needed for both UK IHT and Spanish tax) |
| 🟠 **Soon** | Value the full worldwide estate (UK + Spain + all savings) |
| 🟡 **Before probate** | Complete **IHT400 + IHT417** and pay any UK Inheritance Tax due |
| 🟡 **Before probate** | Apply for UK **Grant of Probate** |
| 🟢 **After probate** | Deal with UK estate (property, bank accounts, etc.) |
| 🟢 **Parallel process** | Spanish lawyer handles the Spanish property transfer separately |

---

### 🧑‍⚖️ Strong Recommendation: Get Professional Help

Given the cross-border nature of this estate, this is genuinely complex. I'd strongly recommend:
- A **UK solicitor** specialising in international or cross-border estates to handle the UK side (IHT400/IHT417 and probate)
- A **Spanish abogado** (lawyer) to handle the Spanish inheritance process – ideally one who works with British clients
- The **Law Society's "Find a Solicitor"** tool can help you find a UK solicitor with international estate experience: 👉 [Find a Solicitor – Law Society](https://solicitors.lawsociety.org.uk/)

The **6-month Spanish deadline** is the most time-sensitive element right now. Don't delay on finding a Spanish lawyer.

💬 Response (13,817 in / 1,549 out)
Good — here's how those two new details change things:

---

## How Savings and Spanish Property Affect Your Journey

---

### 💰 The Savings — Impact on Inheritance Tax

The savings must be included in the **total estate valuation** for Inheritance Tax purposes. This makes it more likely the estate exceeds the tax-free threshold:

| Asset | Notes |
|---|---|
| UK property | Include current market value (get a formal RICS valuation) |
| Savings / bank accounts | Contact each bank for a balance on the date of death |
| Spanish property | **Must also be included** (see below) |

> ⚠️ **Remember:** The IHT-free threshold is **£325,000** (or up to **£500,000** if the UK home passes to children/grandchildren). With property *and* savings *and* overseas assets, you should get a full valuation done promptly.

---

### 🇪🇸 The Spanish Property — This Adds Significant Complexity

This is the most important new factor. Here's what it means:

#### 1. It Must Be Declared for UK Inheritance Tax
Because your mother was **UK domiciled** (lived in the UK), **her worldwide assets are subject to UK Inheritance Tax** — including the Spanish property. You must include its market value in the IHT400 form.

- Get a **formal valuation from a Spanish estate agent or surveyor** (in euros, then convert to GBP at the date-of-death exchange rate)
- Use **HMRC form IHT417** (*Foreign Assets*) alongside the main IHT400

#### 2. Spain Has Its Own Inheritance Tax Too
Spain levies its own *Impuesto de Sucesiones* (Inheritance Tax) on property located in Spain. This means:
- You (or the beneficiary) will likely owe **Spanish inheritance tax** to the Spanish tax authority (*Agencia Tributaria*)
- The rate varies by region — Andalucía, Valencia, etc. all have different rules
- ⚠️ **You will need a Spanish lawyer (*abogado*)** to handle this — it cannot be done through UK government services

> 💡 **Good news on double taxation:** The UK has arrangements to avoid being taxed twice on the same asset. Any Spanish inheritance tax paid can usually be offset against the UK IHT bill on that same property. Keep all receipts and documentation.

#### 3. You Will Need a Separate Spanish Probate Process
A **UK Grant of Probate does not automatically apply in Spain**. You will need:

- The UK Grant of Probate **apostilled** (officially certified for international use) — you can do this via the [Foreign, Commonwealth & Development Office](https://www.gov.uk/get-document-legalised)
- A **Spanish NIE number** (tax identification number) for the beneficiary — apply via a Spanish consulate in the UK or in Spain
- A Spanish lawyer to handle the *escritura* (title deed transfer) at a Spanish notary
- The process typically takes **3–6 months** in Spain and runs **in parallel** with the UK probate process

#### 4. Order Extra Certified Death Certificates
Spain will require **official copies of the UK death certificate**, and they will need to be:
- **Translated into Spanish** by a sworn translator
- **Apostilled** by the FCDO

> 📌 **Practical tip:** Order **at least 2–3 extra** death certificates beyond what you'd need for the UK alone (so 7–8 total). It's much cheaper to order them all at once now than to reorder later.

---

### 📋 Updated Checklist

- [ ] Register the death & order **7–8 certified death certificates**
- [ ] Use Tell Us Once
- [ ] Value **all assets**: UK property, savings (date-of-death balances), and Spanish property
- [ ] Complete **IHT400 + IHT417** (Foreign Assets) for HMRC — pay any tax within 6 months
- [ ] Apply for UK **Grant of Probate** (PA1P or PA1A)
- [ ] Get the Grant of Probate **apostilled** by the FCDO
- [ ] Engage a **Spanish lawyer** to handle Spanish inheritance tax and property transfer
- [ ] Apply for a **Spanish NIE number** for the beneficiary
- [ ] Get death certificate(s) **translated and apostilled** for use in Spain

---

### 🔴 Strong Recommendation: Get Professional Help

Given the combination of:
- UK property requiring probate
- Overseas property in Spain
- Savings potentially pushing the estate over the IHT threshold

...this estate is complex enough that **instructing a UK solicitor with international probate experience** is strongly advisable. They can coordinate with a Spanish *abogado* and ensure nothing is missed across both jurisdictions. Look for a solicitor accredited by the **Society of Trust and Estate Practitioners (STEP)** — [step.org/find-a-member](https://www.step.org/find-a-member).

---

💬 Response (63,561 in / 1,806 out)
Thank you for your patience while I checked the official guidance. Here is a clear picture of what happens to your mother's Pension Credit and what you need to do:

---

## What Happens to Pension Credit After a Death

### 🛑 Pension Credit Stops Immediately on Death
Pension Credit **ends on the date of death**. Your mother was not entitled to any payments made after that date. Because benefits like Pension Credit are often paid in advance or in arrears, there is a real risk that payments have already been made **after she died** — and these will be classed as **overpayments that the estate must repay** to DWP.

---

### ⚠️ Act Quickly – Check for Overpayments
This is time-sensitive. If Pension Credit payments have continued to land in her bank account since her death, **do not spend that money**. It belongs to DWP and will need to be returned. The DWP will calculate exactly what was overpaid once they are notified.

---

### 📋 How to Notify DWP

You have **two ways** to do this:

#### Option 1: Tell Us Once *(Recommended – easiest)*
As covered in our earlier conversation, the **Tell Us Once** service (which you access after registering the death) automatically notifies **DWP** on your behalf. DWP will then:
- Cancel the Pension Credit claim
- Calculate any overpayment
- Write to the executor/administrator of the estate to arrange repayment

#### Option 2: Contact DWP's Pension Service Directly
If you want to notify them immediately (before registering the death or using Tell Us Once), you can contact the **Pension Credit claim line**, which also handles changes of circumstances:
- 📞 **0800 99 1234** (Monday to Friday, 8am to 6pm)
- Relay UK: 18001 then 0800 99 1234
- 👉 [Pension Credit – Report a change of circumstances](https://www.gov.uk/pension-credit/report-a-change-of-circumstances)

---

### 💰 What Else Pension Credit May Have Been "Passporting" To

Because your mother received Pension Credit, she may also have been automatically entitled to a number of **linked benefits** that will also now need to stop. These include:

| Benefit | What Happens |
|--------|-------------|
| **Free TV licence** (if aged 75+) | Cancelled automatically via Tell Us Once |
| **Cold Weather Payments** | No further payments will be made |
| **Warm Home Discount** | Cancelled for future years |
| **Council Tax Reduction** | Local council notified via Tell Us Once |
| **NHS dental/glasses help** | Entitlement ends on date of death |

---

### 💷 Could the Estate Be Owed Any Money?

Possibly, yes. If Pension Credit was paid **in arrears** and there are days between the last payment and the date of death that haven't been paid, the estate may be owed a small final payment. DWP will calculate this when they process the notification.

---

### 🔑 Key Points to Remember

> 1. **Don't spend** any Pension Credit payments received after the date of death — they will need to be returned
> 2. **Tell Us Once** is the simplest way to notify DWP — do this within 28 days of registering the death
> 3. DWP will write to the **executor/administrator** of the estate about any overpayment — this is a debt of the estate, not a personal debt of yours
> 4. Any overpayment must be **settled before the estate is distributed** to beneficiaries

Would you like help with any other aspect of this process?
TREATMENT

💬 Response (40,047 in / 1,224 out)
Yes, this is an important detail. Here's exactly what happens to your mother's Pension Credit, and what you need to do:

---

## What Happens to Your Mother's Pension Credit

### ⚠️ Pension Credit Stops Immediately on Death

Pension Credit is a **personal benefit** — it **ceases automatically on the date of death** and cannot be transferred to anyone else. However, there are several important things to action:

---

### 🔴 Action Required: Notify DWP Promptly

Even though **Tell Us Once** will notify DWP automatically, it's worth also calling the **Pension Service directly** to ensure the Pension Credit claim is closed correctly and to check for any of the following:

- **Overpayments** — if any Pension Credit was paid *after* the date of death (e.g. into her bank account), DWP will ask for it to be repaid from the estate. Don't spend it.
- **Underpayments** — if she was owed any arrears, these can be claimed by the estate.

📞 **Pension Service:** 0800 731 0469 (Mon–Fri, 8am–6pm)

---

### 💡 Important: Pension Credit Was a "Gateway Benefit"

Because your mother received Pension Credit, she may have been receiving several **linked benefits that also now stop**. You should check whether any of the following were in payment and notify the relevant organisations:

| Linked Benefit | Who to Notify |
|---|---|
| **Winter Fuel Payment** | Handled by Tell Us Once / DWP |
| **Warm Home Discount** | Contact her energy supplier |
| **Cold Weather Payments** | Stops automatically |
| **Free TV Licence** (if she was 75+) | Contact TV Licensing: 0300 790 6165 |
| **Council Tax Reduction** | Contact her local council |
| **NHS dental/glasses help** | No action needed — ceases automatically |

> 📌 **Tell Us Once will handle most of these** — but it's worth double-checking with her energy supplier and local council directly, as they don't always receive the notification in time to prevent further payments going out.

---

### 💰 Could Any Money Be Owed *Back* to the Estate?

Possibly, yes. If your mother was **underpaid** Pension Credit at any point (this has affected many pensioners, particularly women), the estate may be owed arrears. DWP has been running a correction exercise. When you call to notify them, ask specifically:

> *"Was my mother's Pension Credit claim correct and up to date? Is any underpayment owed to the estate?"*

---

### 🔍 Check: Was She Entitled to More?

This is also a good moment to check whether she was receiving **everything she was entitled to**. Pension Credit recipients are also eligible for:

- **Housing Benefit** (if she was renting — not applicable here as she owned her home, but worth noting)
- **Support for Mortgage Interest** — if she had a mortgage, this may have been payable and could form part of the estate picture

---

### 📋 Summary: What to Do About the Benefits

- [ ] **Tell Us Once** will notify DWP — do this at the register office appointment
- [ ] **Call the Pension Service (0800 731 0469)** to confirm the claim is closed and check for over/underpayments
- [ ] **Check her bank account** — if any Pension Credit arrived after the date of death, set it aside to repay DWP
- [ ] **Notify her energy supplier** about the Warm Home Discount
- [ ] **Contact her local council** to close her Council Tax Reduction and confirm the property's exempt status while in probate
- [ ] **Contact TV Licensing** if she had a free licence (75+)

---

This all feeds back into the estate administration — any overpayments DWP recovers will reduce the estate value, and any underpayments owed will increase it. Both are relevant to your Inheritance Tax valuation.

Would you like help with anything else — for example, how to handle her bank accounts, or what to do about the property while probate is ongoing?

💬 Response (14,057 in / 1,702 out)
I have everything I need to give you a clear, step-by-step plan. Here's what you should do, in order of priority:

---

## Your Action Plan After Redundancy

### ✅ Step 1 — Check Your Statutory Redundancy Pay (Do This Now)

Because you've worked for your employer for **5 years** (well over the 2-year minimum), you are entitled to **Statutory Redundancy Pay**. The amount depends on your age, length of service, and weekly pay.

👉 **Use the official calculator:** [Calculate your statutory redundancy pay](https://www.gov.uk/calculate-your-redundancy-pay)

**Key facts:**
- Your weekly pay is based on your average earnings over the **12 weeks before your redundancy notice**
- You have **6 months from the date your job ends** to make a claim
- You are also entitled to a **notice period** (at least 5 weeks for 5 years' service) — check whether you were paid in lieu of notice or are still in your notice period
- Your redundancy pay is **tax-free up to £30,000**

If your employer refuses to pay, you can claim through the government's **Redundancy Payments Service**.

---

### ✅ Step 2 — Claim Universal Credit Immediately

**Don't delay this** — Universal Credit takes around **5 weeks to pay out** for the first time, so the sooner you claim, the sooner money arrives. As someone out of work with a mortgage and no savings, you are very likely to be eligible.

👉 **Claim here:** [Universal Credit](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit)

**Important things to know:**
- You can claim **the same day** you become unemployed — don't wait
- If you cannot wait 5 weeks for your first payment, you can request a **Universal Credit Advance** (an interest-free loan repaid from future payments)
- Your **statutory redundancy pay may affect your claim** if it takes you over the £16,000 savings threshold — but since you have no savings, this is worth checking with the DWP directly
- You'll need to agree to a **Claimant Commitment** (e.g. actively looking for work)

---

### ✅ Step 3 — Contact Your Mortgage Lender Right Away

**Do this before you miss any payments.** Lenders are required to treat you fairly and most have hardship provisions. Ask about:
- A **mortgage payment holiday**
- Switching to **interest-only payments** temporarily
- Extending your mortgage term to reduce monthly costs

This is important because government mortgage help (Step 4 below) **cannot cover arrears**, so it's better to act before you fall behind.

---

### ✅ Step 4 — Apply for Support for Mortgage Interest (SMI)

Once you are receiving Universal Credit, you may qualify for **Support for Mortgage Interest (SMI)** — a government loan that helps pay the **interest** on your mortgage.

👉 **Find out more:** [Support for Mortgage Interest (SMI)](https://www.gov.uk/support-for-mortgage-interest)

**Key facts:**
- You must be receiving a **qualifying benefit** (Universal Credit counts) — this is why claiming UC in Step 2 comes first
- It covers **interest only**, not capital repayments or arrears
- It is a **loan**, repaid with interest when you sell or transfer ownership of your home
- You do **not** need to apply separately — the DWP will contact you about SMI once you're on Universal Credit

---

### ✅ Step 5 — Get Free Debt and Financial Advice

Given your mortgage and no savings, it's worth speaking to a free adviser now, before any problems escalate:

- **Citizens Advice** — [citizensadvice.org.uk](https://www.citizensadvice.org.uk) — free advice on benefits, debt, and redundancy rights
- **MoneyHelper** — [moneyhelper.org.uk](https://www.moneyhelper.org.uk) — government-backed financial guidance
- **Shelter** — if you have any concerns about keeping your home

---

## Summary of the Order

| Priority | Action | Where |
|---|---|---|
| 🔴 Urgent | Calculate & confirm redundancy pay | [gov.uk/calculate-your-redundancy-pay](https://www.gov.uk/calculate-your-redundancy-pay) |
| 🔴 Urgent | Claim Universal Credit | [gov.uk/universal-credit](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit) |
| 🔴 Urgent | Call your mortgage lender | Your lender directly |
| 🟡 Soon | Apply for SMI (after UC is in place) | Automatic via DWP |
| 🟡 Soon | Get free financial advice | Citizens Advice / MoneyHelper |

The most important thing is **not to wait** — both Universal Credit and your mortgage lender conversations should happen this week. Would you like more detail on any of these steps?

💬 Response (28,197 in / 2,038 out)
Excellent — I now have a comprehensive picture of everything relevant to your situation. Given that you have a **mortgage**, **no savings**, and were made redundant after **5 years**, here is your personalised step-by-step guide, prioritised by urgency:

---

## 🗂️ Your Redundancy Action Plan

### ⚡ Phase 1 — Do These First (This Week)

---

#### 1. 📄 Get Your P45 from Your Employer
Your employer is **legally required** to give you a P45 on or after your last day. You'll need it for benefit claims and any tax refund.
- If they haven't sent it, chase them immediately.
- If they're unresponsive, contact **HMRC**: 📞 0300 200 3300 (Mon–Fri, 8am–6pm)
- 🔗 [GOV.UK: P45 guidance](https://www.gov.uk/paye-forms-p45-p60-p11d/p45)

---

#### 2. 💷 Claim Your Statutory Redundancy Pay
With **5 years' service**, you are entitled to Statutory Redundancy Pay. Your employer must pay this — it's calculated based on your age, weekly pay (capped at £643/week), and years of service.
- Use the [GOV.UK redundancy pay calculator](https://www.gov.uk/claim-redundancy) to check your entitlement.
- If your employer refuses, you can take them to an **Employment Tribunal** (see below).
- 🔗 [GOV.UK: Redundancy Pay](https://www.gov.uk/redundancy-payments-helpline)

---

#### 3. 💰 Claim Universal Credit — **Urgently**
As you have no savings and a mortgage, this is your most important financial lifeline. UC is the main out-of-work benefit and includes a **housing element** that can help with mortgage interest (see point 5).
- Apply online immediately — payments take ~5 weeks to arrive, so don't delay.
- You'll need your P45, bank details, and tenancy/mortgage details.
- Standard allowance: **£400.14/month** (if you're 25+, single)
- 📞 UC Helpline: 0800 328 5644 (Mon–Fri, 8am–6pm)
- 🔗 [Apply for Universal Credit](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit/how-to-claim)

---

#### 4. 🏠 Support for Mortgage Interest (SMI) — Critical for You
Because you have a mortgage and no savings, this is **especially important**. Once you're on UC (or New Style JSA/ESA), you can apply for an **SMI loan** to cover your mortgage interest payments.
- It's a government loan secured against your property, repaid when you sell.
- Interest rate used: 2.36% (2025–26). Capital limit: £200,000.
- 📞 Jobcentre Plus: 0800 169 0140
- 🔗 [GOV.UK: Support for Mortgage Interest](https://www.gov.uk/support-for-mortgage-interest)

> ⚠️ **Also contact your mortgage lender now** — most lenders have hardship/forbearance policies and may offer a payment holiday. This is separate from SMI and can provide immediate relief.

---

#### 5. 📋 New Style Jobseeker's Allowance (JSA)
With 5 years of employment, you almost certainly have enough **National Insurance contributions** to qualify. New Style JSA can be claimed **alongside Universal Credit** and pays up to **£92.05/week** for up to 6 months.
- You'll need your P45 to claim.
- 🔗 [Apply for New Style JSA](https://www.gov.uk/jobseekers-allowance/apply-new-style-jsa)

---

#### 6. 🏛️ Council Tax Reduction
Apply to your **local council** for a reduction on your Council Tax bill — this can reduce it significantly or even to zero on a low income.
- 🔗 [Find your local council](https://www.gov.uk/find-local-council)
- 🔗 [Apply for Council Tax Reduction](https://www.gov.uk/apply-council-tax-reduction)

---

#### 7. 💸 Claim an Income Tax Refund (P50)
Since you were made redundant mid-tax year and may not return to work before 5 April, you've likely **overpaid income tax** through PAYE. You can claim this back now.
- You'll need your P45 first.
- 🔗 [Claim a tax refund](https://www.gov.uk/claim-tax-refund)

---

#### 8. 🛡️ National Insurance Credits
Once you're on UC or New Style JSA, **NI credits are awarded automatically** — this protects your State Pension record while you're not working. No action needed beyond claiming your benefits.
- 🔗 [GOV.UK: NI Credits](https://www.gov.uk/national-insurance-credits)

---

### 💡 Also Worth Knowing

| Service | What it does | Link |
|---|---|---|
| **NHS Low Income Scheme (HC2)** | Free/reduced prescriptions, dental & sight tests | [Apply](https://www.gov.uk/nhs-low-income-scheme) |
| **Social Tariff Broadband** | Discounted broadband (~£12–20/month) for UC claimants | [Check](https://www.gov.uk/affordable-broadband) |
| **Breathing Space** | 60-day legal protection from creditor action while you get debt advice | [Info](https://www.gov.uk/options-for-dealing-with-your-debts/breathing-space) |
| **Find a Job** | DWP's free national job search service | [Search](https://findajob.dwp.gov.uk) |

---

### ⚖️ If Your Redundancy Was Unfair

If you believe your redundancy was handled unlawfully (e.g. unfair selection, no proper process, unpaid wages), you have **3 months minus 1 day** from your last day to act:

1. **ACAS Early Conciliation** — Free, mandatory first step before any tribunal claim. Contact ACAS immediately to preserve your deadline. 📞 [acas.org.uk/early-conciliation](https://www.acas.org.uk/early-conciliation)
2. **Employment Tribunal** — If conciliation fails, you can file a formal claim. 🔗 [GOV.UK: Employment Tribunals](https://www.gov.uk/employment-tribunals)

---

### 🔑 Your Priority Order This Week

1. ✅ Chase your **P45**
2. ✅ Apply for **Universal Credit** (don't wait — 5-week wait starts from claim date)
3. ✅ Apply for **New Style JSA** alongside UC
4. ✅ Calculate and claim your **Statutory Redundancy Pay**
5. ✅ Contact your **mortgage lender** about a payment holiday
6. ✅ Apply for **Council Tax Reduction** at your local council
7. ✅ Claim your **income tax refund** (P50) once you have your P45
8. ✅ Ask DWP about **Support for Mortgage Interest** once your UC claim is active

Would you like more detail on any of these steps, or do you have any specific circumstances (e.g. health conditions, children, location in the UK) that might unlock additional support?

💬 Response (21,501 in / 1,455 out)
Yes, being signed off with stress and anxiety makes a significant difference to your situation. Here's how it changes things:

---

## How Your Fit Note Changes Your Position

### ⚠️ Statutory Sick Pay (SSP) — Unfortunately Not Available to You

Normally, if you're signed off sick, your employer pays you SSP (currently **£116.75/week**). However, because you were **made redundant last Friday, you no longer have an employer** — so you cannot claim SSP. This is an important gap to be aware of.

---

### ✅ New Change: Claim **New Style ESA** as Well as Universal Credit

Because you have a fit note and have paid National Insurance contributions (which you almost certainly have after 5 years of employment), you should now **also claim New Style Employment and Support Allowance (ESA)** alongside Universal Credit.

👉 **Claim here:** [New Style ESA](https://www.gov.uk/employment-support-allowance/how-to-claim)

**Why this matters:**
- New Style ESA is based on your **National Insurance record**, not your savings or income — so it's separate from Universal Credit
- You can receive **both New Style ESA and Universal Credit at the same time** (though your UC will be reduced by the ESA amount, you benefit from receiving ESA because it earns you **Class 1 NI credits** towards your State Pension)
- During the first 13 weeks (the "assessment period") you'll receive up to **£92.05/week** if you're 25 or over
- After assessment, you'll be placed in either the **Work-Related Activity Group** (up to £92.05/week) or the **Support Group** (up to £140.55/week) depending on how your condition affects you

---

### ✅ Key Change to Your Universal Credit Claim: Report Your Fit Note

When you claim Universal Credit, you must **tell them you have been signed off by your GP**. This is very important because:

- You will be assessed for **"Limited Capability for Work"** — which means your **Claimant Commitment will be reduced or removed**
- Instead of being required to actively job-search, you will likely only need to **focus on your health and recovery**
- You will **not be sanctioned** for not looking for work while you are signed off
- Upload or report your fit note through your **UC online journal** as soon as you have it

---

### 📋 Updated Action Plan

| Priority | Action | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| 🔴 Urgent | Claim **Universal Credit** | Do this immediately |
| 🔴 Urgent | Claim **New Style ESA** | Do this at the same time — don't delay |
| 🔴 Urgent | **Report your fit note** to UC | Reduces your job-seeking obligations while you're unwell |
| 🔴 Urgent | Contact your **mortgage lender** | Before you miss any payments |
| 🟡 Soon | Confirm **redundancy pay** entitlement | [gov.uk/calculate-your-redundancy-pay](https://www.gov.uk/calculate-your-redundancy-pay) |
| 🟡 Soon | **SMI** (Support for Mortgage Interest) | Automatic once UC is in place |
| 🟡 Soon | Seek **mental health support** | Your GP can refer you — ask about NHS Talking Therapies |

---

### 💛 One More Thing — Your Mental Health

Being made redundant is a recognised cause of significant stress and anxiety, and you're clearly dealing with a lot at once. As well as the financial steps above:

- Ask your GP about a referral to **NHS Talking Therapies** (free, no waiting list in many areas)
- **Mind** ([mind.org.uk](https://www.mind.org.uk)) has specific guidance on money worries and mental health
- **Citizens Advice** can also help reduce the stress of navigating all of this

You don't have to manage all of this alone. Would you like more detail on any of these steps?

💬 Response (50,247 in / 1,835 out)
Yes — being signed off with stress and anxiety changes your situation significantly, and in several important ways. Here's a focused update to your plan:

---

## 🏥 How Your GP Sign-Off Changes Things

### 🔄 Key Change: JSA → ESA

Being signed off means you **cannot be required to look for work**, which means **New Style JSA is no longer the right benefit** — you should claim **New Style Employment and Support Allowance (ESA)** instead.

> ⚠️ **You can still claim both Universal Credit AND New Style ESA simultaneously** — they work together, just as JSA would have.

---

### 1. 📋 New Style ESA — Claim This Instead of JSA

**New Style ESA** is specifically for people whose health condition prevents or limits their ability to work. With 5 years of employment, you almost certainly have enough NI contributions to qualify.

- **Rate:** Up to **£92.05/week** (if you're 25+)
- You'll need your **fit note from your GP** — keep getting these renewed
- You'll be asked to undergo a **Work Capability Assessment (WCA)** — a medical assessment to determine how your condition affects your ability to work
- 📞 ESA Helpline: **0800 055 6688** (Mon–Fri, 8am–6pm)
- 🔗 [Apply for New Style ESA](https://www.gov.uk/employment-support-allowance/how-to-claim)

---

### 2. 📄 Submit Your Fit Note to DWP

Once you've claimed ESA or UC, you must submit your GP's fit note to DWP to support your claim. You can do this digitally:

- 🔗 [Submit your fit note online](https://send-fit-note.service.gov.uk/)
- Keep getting your fit note **renewed by your GP** for as long as you remain signed off

---

### 3. 💰 UC Health Element — A Major Financial Boost

Because you're signed off, you may qualify for the **Limited Capability for Work and Work-Related Activity (LCWRA)** element of Universal Credit. This is an **additional £423.27/month** on top of your standard UC allowance.

- This is assessed through the same **Work Capability Assessment**
- While waiting for the WCA, report your health condition via your **UC journal** and submit your fit note
- 🔗 [UC health element info](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit/what-youll-get)

> 💡 **Combined**, your UC could be: £400.14 (standard) + £423.27 (LCWRA) = **~£823/month** — significantly more than without the health element.

---

### 4. 🧠 Consider Claiming PIP

Stress and anxiety can qualify for **Personal Independence Payment (PIP)** if your condition affects your daily living or mobility. PIP is:
- **Not means-tested** — it doesn't matter what other income or benefits you have
- **Not affected by working or not working**
- Worth up to **£110.40/week** (daily living enhanced) + **£77.05/week** (mobility enhanced)

PIP is assessed on how your condition affects you day-to-day, not on the diagnosis itself. Many people with anxiety and depression successfully claim PIP.

- 📞 PIP helpline: **0800 917 2222** (Mon–Fri, 8am–5pm)
- 🔗 [Apply for PIP](https://www.gov.uk/pip/how-to-claim)

> 💡 **Claiming PIP also unlocks** free prescriptions, a Disabled Persons Railcard (1/3 off rail fares), and potentially a Council Tax disability reduction.

---

### 5. 💊 Free NHS Prescriptions

If you're prescribed medication for your stress/anxiety (e.g. antidepressants), you may be entitled to **free prescriptions** once you're receiving ESA or UC with the health element. Declare your benefit status at the pharmacy.

- 🔗 [Free prescriptions info](https://www.gov.uk/get-free-prescriptions-on-the-nhs)

---

### 6. 🚗 DVLA — Check if You Need to Notify Them

If your stress and anxiety significantly affects your ability to drive safely, you may have a **legal obligation to notify the DVLA**. This is worth checking — failure to notify can invalidate your car insurance.

- 🔗 [Check if your condition is notifiable](https://www.gov.uk/health-conditions-and-driving)

---

### 7. 🏠 Care Needs Assessment

If your condition is significantly affecting your ability to manage daily life at home, you can request a **free Care Needs Assessment** from your local council. This can unlock practical support and funded help.

- 🔗 [Request a care needs assessment](https://www.gov.uk/care-needs-assessment-adults)

---

## 📋 Updated Priority Order

| Priority | Action |
|---|---|
| ✅ 1 | Get your **P45** from your employer |
| ✅ 2 | Apply for **Universal Credit** — don't delay |
| ✅ 3 | Apply for **New Style ESA** (not JSA — you're signed off) |
| ✅ 4 | **Submit your fit note** to DWP online |
| ✅ 5 | Report your health condition via your **UC journal** to trigger LCWRA assessment |
| ✅ 6 | Claim **Statutory Redundancy Pay** from your employer |
| ✅ 7 | Contact your **mortgage lender** about a payment holiday |
| ✅ 8 | Apply for **Council Tax Reduction** at your local council |
| ✅ 9 | Start a **PIP claim** — this takes time, so begin now |
| ✅ 10 | Claim your **income tax refund** (P50) once you have your P45 |
| ✅ 11 | Ask DWP about **Support for Mortgage Interest** once UC is active |

---

### 💬 One More Thing — Your Mental Health

Being made redundant and dealing with a health condition simultaneously is genuinely hard. As well as the financial support above, please know that:

- Your GP can refer you to **NHS talking therapies (IAPT)** — free CBT and counselling
- **Mind** (mind.org.uk) and **Samaritans** (116 123, free, 24/7) offer support
- **Citizens Advice** can help you navigate all of the above for free: [citizensadvice.org.uk](https://www.citizensadvice.org.uk)

Would you like more detail on any of these, or do you have children, a partner, or other circumstances that might unlock further support?

💬 Response (25,027 in / 1,222 out)
I now have enough information to give you a clear and accurate answer. Here's how your £12,000 redundancy payment affects things:

---

## How Your £12,000 Redundancy Payment Affects Your Benefits

### ✅ New Style ESA — **Not Affected At All**

Good news here: your redundancy payment has **absolutely no effect** on New Style ESA. This benefit is based entirely on your **National Insurance contributions record**, not your savings or capital. You should still claim this immediately.

---

### ⚠️ Universal Credit — **Affected, But You're Still Eligible**

Universal Credit has a **capital (savings) threshold system**:

| Amount in savings/capital | Effect on UC |
|---|---|
| **Under £6,000** | No effect on UC payments |
| **£6,000 – £16,000** | UC is **reduced** via "tariff income" |
| **Over £16,000** | You **cannot claim** UC at all |

Your £12,000 redundancy payment puts you in the **middle band**. This means:

- You **can still claim Universal Credit** ✅
- But your payments will be **reduced** — the DWP treats every **£250 (or part thereof) over £6,000** as if it generates **£4.35/month of "tariff income"**
- On £12,000, that's £6,000 over the threshold = **24 × £4.35 = approximately £104/month deducted** from your UC
- **Crucially, as you spend the money** (on mortgage payments, bills, food etc.), your capital will fall and your UC payments will **increase accordingly**

> ⚠️ **You must declare the £12,000 to the DWP when you claim** — failing to do so could be treated as fraud. Report it honestly and your payments will simply be adjusted.

---

### ✅ Support for Mortgage Interest (SMI) — **Not Affected**

SMI eligibility is based on receiving a qualifying benefit (Universal Credit), not on your savings level. Your redundancy payment does **not** disqualify you from SMI.

---

### 💡 One Important Practical Point: Don't Spend the Money Recklessly

The DWP has rules around **"deprivation of capital"** — if you spend or give away money specifically to bring yourself below the £6,000 threshold and increase your UC, they can treat you as still having it. Spending it on **genuine living costs** (mortgage, bills, food) is completely fine and expected.

---

### 📋 Updated Summary

| Benefit | Effect of £12,000 redundancy pay |
|---|---|
| **New Style ESA** | ✅ No effect — claim immediately |
| **Universal Credit** | ⚠️ Eligible, but ~£104/month reduction until savings fall below £6,000 |
| **Support for Mortgage Interest** | ✅ No effect |

---

### 🔑 The Bottom Line

Your £12,000 is **well below the £16,000 cut-off**, so you are still entitled to claim both New Style ESA and Universal Credit. The redundancy pay will reduce your UC slightly for now, but that reduction will decrease naturally as you use the money for living costs. **Claim both benefits this week** — don't wait.
