I now have everything I need to give your wife a comprehensive and accurate guide. Here it is:

---

## 👩 Support Available for Your Wife as Your Full-Time Carer

Your wife is entitled to significant support in her own right. Here's everything she should apply for and do, in order of priority.

---

## Step 1: Carer's Allowance — The Main Financial Benefit

**[Carer's Allowance](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance)** is the main benefit for people who provide regular, substantial care. It is currently worth **£83.30 per week**.

### Eligibility — she must meet ALL of these:
- ✅ Aged 16 or over
- ✅ Caring for you for **at least 35 hours a week** (which as a full-time carer she almost certainly does)
- ✅ **You must already be receiving** PIP (daily living component), Attendance Allowance, or another qualifying disability benefit — this is why claiming PIP or Attendance Allowance for you first is so important
- ✅ Her earnings are **£196 or less per week** after tax, NI and expenses
- ✅ Not in full-time education (21+ hours/week of study)
- ✅ Normally lives in England, Scotland or Wales

### Important things to know:
- **If she receives State Pension** that is £83.30/week or more, she cannot receive Carer's Allowance on top — but she may still be able to get an **underlying entitlement** which can boost Pension Credit
- Claiming Carer's Allowance **may affect your benefits** — specifically, if you receive a **Severe Disability Premium** as part of any benefit, that could be reduced or stopped. It's worth using a **[benefits calculator](https://www.gov.uk/benefits-calculators)** before claiming to check the overall household impact
- She will **not be affected by the benefit cap**
- If she also receives **Universal Credit**, it will be reduced by the amount of Carer's Allowance — but she may get an **extra carer element** added to her Universal Credit

### 🏴󠁧󠁢󠁳󠁣󠁴󠁿 If you live in Scotland:
She should apply for **[Carer Support Payment](https://www.mygov.scot/carer-support-payment)** instead, which is the Scottish equivalent.

### How to apply:
📱 Apply online at **[gov.uk/carers-allowance/make-a-claim](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance/make-a-claim)**, or use paper form **DS700**
📞 Helpline: **0800 731 0297** (Monday–Friday, 8am–6pm)

---

## Step 2: Carer's Credit — Protect Her State Pension

Even if your wife doesn't qualify for Carer's Allowance (e.g. because she receives a State Pension above the threshold), she should claim **[Carer's Credit](https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit)**.

- This is a **National Insurance credit** that fills gaps in her NI record, protecting her entitlement to the **full State Pension**
- Requires caring for **at least 20 hours a week** (easily met as a full-time carer)
- **Free to claim** — no income or savings limits
- If she already gets Carer's Allowance, she gets NI credits **automatically** and does not need to claim Carer's Credit separately
- She can still get Carer's Credit during **breaks in caring of up to 12 weeks** (e.g. if you go into hospital)

---

## Step 3: Request a Carer's Assessment

Under the **Care Act 2014**, your wife has a **legal right** to a free **Carer's Assessment** from your local council, regardless of her financial situation or how much care she provides.

This assessment looks at **her own wellbeing and needs** — not just yours — and can unlock:
- **Respite care** — temporary care arranged for you so she can take a break
- **Replacement care** — someone to step in while she rests, attends appointments, or has time for herself
- Help with **her own health, work, or social life**
- **Direct Payments** for her to arrange her own support
- Signposting to local carer support groups and services

### How to request it:
Contact your **local council's adult social services** department and ask for a Carer's Assessment. You can find your local council at **[gov.uk/find-local-council](https://www.gov.uk/find-local-council)**.

---

## Step 4: Additional Financial Support

Depending on your household circumstances, your wife may also be able to access:

| Benefit | What it is | Link |
|---|---|---|
| **Universal Credit** | Top-up for low income households — includes a **carer element** of ~£198/month | [gov.uk/universal-credit](https://www.gov.uk/universal-credit) |
| **Pension Credit** | If she is over State Pension age and on a low income — includes a **carer addition** | [gov.uk/pension-credit](https://www.gov.uk/pension-credit) |
| **Council Tax Reduction** | Discount on Council Tax based on income | Contact your local council |

---

## Step 5: Her Wellbeing — Respite and Support

Caring full-time is physically and emotionally demanding. It's important your wife also looks after herself:

- **Respite care** (arranged through the Carer's Assessment) gives her regular breaks
- **[Carers UK](https://www.carersuk.org)** — the national charity for carers, with advice, a helpline, and local support groups
- **[Parkinson's UK](https://www.parkinsons.org.uk)** — has dedicated support for carers of people with Parkinson's, including a helpline: **0808 800 0303**

---

## Summary Checklist for Your Wife

| Priority | Action |
|---|---|
| 🔴 First | Make sure **you** have claimed PIP or Attendance Allowance (needed to unlock Carer's Allowance) |
| 🔴 Then | Claim **Carer's Allowance** (or Carer Support Payment in Scotland) |
| 🟠 Also | Claim **Carer's Credit** if not getting Carer's Allowance — protects her State Pension |
| 🟠 Soon | Request a **Carer's Assessment** from your local council |
| 🟡 As needed | Check entitlement to **Universal Credit / Pension Credit / Council Tax Reduction** |
| 🟢 Ongoing | Access **respite care** and carer support services for her own wellbeing |

---

The most important prerequisite is that **you have an active PIP or Attendance Allowance claim**, as this is what unlocks Carer's Allowance for your wife. If you haven't already applied for one of those, that should be the very first step. Would you like help with that, or any other aspect of this?

💬 Response (22,557 in / 1,955 out)
Here is a full breakdown of everything your wife is entitled to:

---

# 👩‍❤️‍👨 Support Available for Your Wife as a Full-Time Carer

As someone caring for you full-time, your wife has a substantial set of rights and entitlements in her own name. Here's everything she should know about:

---

## 💷 1. Carer's Allowance — Her Main Benefit

**£83.30 per week** — this is the cornerstone benefit for carers.

| | |
|---|---|
| **Eligibility** | Caring 35+ hours/week for someone receiving PIP (Daily Living component at either rate) or Attendance Allowance |
| **Means-tested?** | ❌ No — but there is an **earnings limit** (currently £151/week net after deductions) |
| **How to claim** | Online at [gov.uk/carers-allowance/how-to-claim](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance/how-to-claim) |
| **Phone** | **0800 731 0297** (Mon–Fri 8am–6pm) |

> ⚠️ **Important — the "overlapping benefits" rule:** If your wife receives her own State Pension (or certain other benefits) that is equal to or more than £83.30/week, she **cannot be paid** Carer's Allowance at the same time. However, she should **still claim it** — she will receive an "underlying entitlement" which unlocks other benefits (see below). Don't let this put her off applying!

---

## 💰 2. Universal Credit — Carer Element (if on UC)

If your wife is on **Universal Credit**, she is entitled to an extra **£201.68/month** added to her UC — the "Carer Element". She doesn't even need to be *receiving* Carer's Allowance — just eligible for it. She simply needs to report her caring role via her UC journal.

---

## 🏦 3. Carer's Credit — Protecting Her State Pension

Even if your wife **can't receive Carer's Allowance** (e.g. due to the overlapping benefits rule), she should claim **Carer's Credit** to protect her National Insurance record and future State Pension entitlement.

| | |
|---|---|
| **What it does** | Fills NI gaps for years spent caring (20+ hours/week) |
| **Cost** | Free |
| **How to claim** | By post using form **CA9176** — download from [gov.uk/carers-credit](https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit) |
| **Phone** | **0300 200 3500** |

> 💡 If she *is* receiving Carer's Allowance, NI credits are applied automatically — she doesn't need to claim Carer's Credit separately.

---

## 🏥 4. Carer's Assessment — Her Own Support Plan

Your wife is entitled to a **free Carer's Assessment** from your local council — completely separate from your own Care Needs Assessment. This is for *her* needs, not yours.

The assessment can unlock:
- **Respite care** — so she can take breaks
- **Local carer support groups and services**
- **One-off grants** from the local authority
- **Emotional and practical support**

| | |
|---|---|
| **How to request** | Contact your local council's Adult Social Care team → [gov.uk/find-local-council](https://www.gov.uk/find-local-council) |
| **Free helpline** | **Carers UK: 0808 808 7777** |

---

## 💼 5. Carer's Leave (if she is also employed)

If your wife has any paid employment alongside caring for you, she has a **statutory legal right** (since April 2024) to:

- **5 days unpaid leave per year** to provide or arrange care
- Available from **day one** of employment — no qualifying period
- Can be taken as individual days or half days
- Her employer **cannot refuse** this — it is a legal right

More details: [gov.uk/carers-leave](https://www.gov.uk/carers-leave)

---

## ⚖️ 6. Lasting Power of Attorney — Act Now While You Can

This is proactively flagged as important for your situation. A **Lasting Power of Attorney (LPA)** is a legal document that allows your wife (or another trusted person) to make decisions on your behalf if you lose mental capacity in the future — which can happen with Parkinson's disease.

There are **two types** — you should consider both:

| Type | What it covers | When it can be used |
|---|---|---|
| **Property & Financial Affairs** | Bank accounts, bills, property, investments | Can be used immediately (with your permission) or when you lose capacity |
| **Health & Welfare** | Medical treatment, care decisions, where you live | Only when you lack mental capacity |

| | |
|---|---|
| **Cost** | **£82 per LPA** (£164 for both) — fee remission available if on low income |
| **How to set up** | Online at [lastingpowerofattorney.service.gov.uk](https://www.lastingpowerofattorney.service.gov.uk/start) |
| **Phone** | Office of the Public Guardian: **0300 456 0300** (Mon–Fri 9am–5pm) |

> ⚠️ **Act sooner rather than later.** An LPA must be set up and registered **while you still have mental capacity**. It cannot be created after capacity is lost. This is one of the most important things you can do as a couple right now.

---

## 📋 Your Wife's Action Checklist

- [ ] **1. Claim Carer's Allowance** → [gov.uk/carers-allowance/how-to-claim](https://www.gov.uk/carers-allowance/how-to-claim) *(even if State Pension may overlap — claim anyway for underlying entitlement)*
- [ ] **2. Request a Carer's Assessment** from your local council → [gov.uk/find-local-council](https://www.gov.uk/find-local-council)
- [ ] **3. If on Universal Credit** — report caring role via UC journal to receive the £201.68/month Carer Element
- [ ] **4. If Carer's Allowance is not payable** — claim Carer's Credit to protect her State Pension → [gov.uk/carers-credit](https://www.gov.uk/carers-credit)
- [ ] **5. Set up Lasting Power of Attorney** (both types) while you have capacity → [lastingpowerofattorney.service.gov.uk](https://www.lastingpowerofattorney.service.gov.uk/start)
- [ ] **6. If employed** — be aware of her right to 5 days Carer's Leave per year → [gov.uk/carers-leave](https://www.gov.uk/carers-leave)

---

> 💡 **Carers UK** ([carersuk.org](https://www.carersuk.org)) and **Parkinson's UK** (**0808 800 0303**) both offer free specialist advice for carers in your wife's situation — they can help her navigate the benefits system and find local support.

Would you like more detail on any of these — for example, the LPA process, or what happens with Carer's Allowance if your wife also receives a State Pension?
